Eggeling
  1. Praj─Бpati set his mind upon Agni’s forms. He searched for that boy (Kum─Бra) who had entered

into the (different) forms. Agni became aware of it,–‘Surely, Father Praj─Бpati is searching for me: well then, let me be suchlike that he knows me not.’

Eggeling
  1. He considered, ‘They are Agni: I will fit them unto mine own self 1. Even as Agni, when kindled, glares, so their eye glares; even as Agni’s smoke rises upwards, so vapour rises from them; even as Agni consumes what is put in him, so they devour; even as Agni’s ashes fall down, so do their faeces: they are indeed Agni; I will fit them unto mine own self.’ He meant to slaughter them for different deities: the Purusha (man) for Vi┼Ыvakarman, the horse for Varuс╣Зa, the bull for Indra, the ram for Tvashс╣нr╠е, the he-goat for Agni.

рд╕ рдРрдХреНрд╖рдд- рдирд╛рдирд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╜рдЗрджрдВ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рднреНрдп рдЖрд▓рд┐рдкреНрд╕реЗ ред рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрд░реНрд╡рд╣рдВ рд░реВрдкрд╛рдгрд┐ рдХрд╛рдордпреЗ- рд╣рдиреНрддреИрдирд╛рдирдЧреНрдирд┐рднреНрдпрдГ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдпрд╛рд▓рднрд╛ рд╜рдЗрддрд┐ ред рддрд╛рдирдЧреНрдирд┐рднреНрдпрдГ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдпрд╛рд▓рднрдд ред рддрджреН рдпрджрдЧреНрдирд┐рднреНрдп рдЗрддрд┐- рдмрд╣реВрдирд┐ рд╣реНрдпрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реВрдкрд╛рдгреНрдпрднреНрдпрдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрддреН ред рдЕрде рдпрддреНрдХрд╛рдорд╛рдпреЗрддрд┐- рдХрд╛рдореЗрди рд╣реНрдпрд╛рд▓рднрдд, рддрд╛рдирд╛рдкреНрд░реАрддрд╛рдиреН рдкрд░реНрдпрдЧреНрдирд┐рдХреГрддрд╛рдиреБрджреАрдЪреЛ рдиреАрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рдордЬреНрдЮрдкрдпрддреН рее рем рее

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

рд╕ рдРрдХреНрд╖рдд рдирд╛рдиреЗрддрд┐ ред ‘рд╕рдГ’ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рдГ рдПрд╡рдВ рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░рд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдиреН- рдХрд┐рдорд░реНрдердВ ? ‘рдирд╛рдирд╛’ рдмрд╣реНрд╡реАрднреНрдпрдГ ‘рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рднреНрдпрдГ’ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрднреНрдпрдГ рдЖрд▓рдмреНрдзреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдорд┐ (‘рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ рдЙ рдЕрд╣рдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрджрдЪреНрдЫреЗрджрдГ) рдЕрд╣рдореБ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрд░реЗрд╡ ‘рд░реВрдкрд╛рдгрд┐’ рдХрд╛рдордпреЗ рд╣рдиреНрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рд╛рдзреНрдпрд╕рд╛рдзрдирдпреЛрд░реНрд╡реИрдпрдзрд┐рдХрд░рдгреНрдпрдЬрдирд┐рддреЗ рдЖрд╢реНрдЪрд░реНрдпреЗ ред ‘рдПрдирд╛рдиреН’ рдкрд╢реВрдиреН ‘рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдп’ рдХрд╛рдордЧреБрдгрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдп ‘рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рднреНрдпрдГ’ рдЕрдЧреНрдирдпреЗ ‘рдЖрд▓рднреЗ’- ‘рдЗрддрд┐’ рдРрдХреНрд╖рддреЗрддреНрдпрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ ред рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдпрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рднреНрдп рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдзрд┐рдХрд░рдгреНрдпреЗ рдХрдердордЧреНрдирд┐рднреНрдп рдЗрддрд┐ рдмрд╣реБрд╡рдЪрдирдореН ? рддрддреНрд░рд╛рд╣- рддрджреН рдпрджрдЧреНрдирд┐рднреНрдп рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реВрдкрд╛рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдмрд╣реБрд╡рдЪрдирдореН ред ‘рддрд╛рдиреН’ рдЕрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЧреБрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдЖрдкреНрд░реАрддрд╛рдирд┐рддрд┐ ред рдкреНрд░рдпрд╛рдЬрдпрд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рд░рд╛рдкреНрд░реАрднрд┐рдГ рдкрд░реНрдпрдЧреНрдирд┐рдХрд░рдгреЗрди рдЪ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХреГрддрд╛рдиреН, рддрджрдирдиреНрддрд░рдореЗрд╡ ‘рдЙрджреАрдЪреЛ рдиреАрддреНрд╡рд╛’ рд╢рд╛рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдкреНрд░рджреЗрд╢рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпреНрдпреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред ‘рд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрдкрдирдВ’ 2 рдирд╛рдо рдорд╛рд░рдгрдореН ред рдорд╛рд░рдгрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдирдпреЗрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее рем рее

Eggeling
  1. He considered, ‘For different deities, indeed, I mean to slaughter now; but I myself desire (kam)

Agni’s forms: well then, I will slaughter them for the Agnis, as for the (object of my) desire.’ He slaughtered them for the Agnis, as for (his) desire,–to wit, ‘for the Agnis,’ because many were the forms of Agni he had set his mind upon; and ‘for the desire,’ because it was with a desire that he slaughtered them. Having appeased them and carried the fire round them, he led them northwards and slew them.

Eggeling
  1. He considered, ‘Those glories (signs of excellence 5) upon which I have set my mind are contained in the heads: well then, I will only put on the heads 6.’ He cut off the heads and put them on (himself, or the altar). The remaining trunks he then let float on the water 7, and brought the sacrifice to its completion by means of (the offering of) a he-goat, thinking, ‘Lest my sacrifice be pulled to pieces.’ After performing that animal sacrifice, Praj─Бpati saw that he had not yet reached the end of Agni (the fire-altar).

Eggeling
  1. He considered, ‘I must search for that body 8 which I let float on the water.’ He searched for it; and what (part) of those (bodies) cast into the water had settled therein, that water he gathered; and what (had settled) in this earth, that clay (he gathered) 9. And having gathered both that clay

and water, he made a brick: hence a brick consists of these two, clay and water.

Eggeling
  1. He considered, ‘Surely, if I fit 10 this (matter) such as it is unto mine own self, I shall become a mortal carcase, not freed from evil: well then, I will bake it by means of the fire.’ So saying, he baked it by means of the fire, and thereby made it immortal; for the sacrificial food which is baked by fire is indeed immortal (or, ambrosia). Hence they bake the bricks with fire: they thereby make them immortal.

Eggeling
  1. And inasmuch as he saw them after offering (ishс╣нv─Б) the animal, therefore they are bricks (ishс╣нak─Б). Eggeling
  1. As to those glories, they are these same heads of the victims; and those (headless) trunks are these five layers (of the fire-altar): thus when he builds up the layers after putting on the heads of the victims, he thereby unites those trunks with those heads.

Eggeling
  1. And because Agni is all those animal victims, therefore animals delight (being) near the fire 12,–

there animals sport with animals. Hence the (sacrificial) fire is set up with him who possesses cattle; for inasmuch as Agni (was) the same as cattle, therefore Praj─Бpati (the lord of creatures or generation) became Agni.

Eggeling
  1. Here now some say, ‘It is at this (point of the performance) that he should offer up all those (five) victims; for had Praj─Бpati then offered up all of them, he would certainly have reached the end of the fire (altar): hence were he (the Sacrificer) now to offer up all those (victims) he would certainly reach the end of the fire (altar).’ Let him not do so: he thus would stray from where the gods have gone, he would stray from the path;–and what would he then gather 15? For those same bodies, those layers, he gathers: let him therefore not do so.

Eggeling
  1. Now when he slaughters those animals, he prepares a home for Agni; for nowhere but in his home does one enjoy himself. But the home means food: it is that he lays down in, front, and when Agni sees that, he turns unto him.

Eggeling
  1. There are a man, a horse, a bull, a ram, and a he-goat; for such are all the animals (used for sacrifice). Animals are food: he thus lays down in front whatever food there is; and seeing that, Agni turns unto him.

  1. There are five; for there are those five Agnis,

Eggeling
  1. A man (purusha) he slaughters first, for man is the first of animals; then a horse, for the horse comes after man; then a bull, for the bull (or cow) comes after the horse; then a ram, for the sheep comes after the cow; then a he-goat, for the goat comes after the sheep: thus he slaughters them according to their form, according to their excellence.

Eggeling
  1. Their ropes may be unequal; that of the man being the longest, then shorter and shorter: thus he makes the ropes according to the form of the animals, to avoid confusion between good and bad. But let them be all alike, all similar; for all these victims are alike, all similar, for they are (all) called Agnis, they are called food: hence they are alike and similar.

Eggeling
  1. Here now they say, ‘How is that complete five-bricked fire of his gained in the animals?’–Well, in the kap─Бlas of the sacrificial cakes that first brick, the earthen one, is obtained; and when he slaughters the animal, thereby the animal brick is obtained, and when two gold chips are (placed) on both sides of the omentum, thereby the gold brick is obtained; and what firewood, stake, and enclosing sticks there are, thereby the wooden brick is obtained; and what ghee, sprinkling-water, and cake there are, thereby the fifth brick, the food, is

obtained: thus then that complete five-bricked fire of his is gained in the animals.

Eggeling
  1. For these (victims) there are twenty-four kindling-verses 17; for the year consists of twenty-four half-moons, and Agni is the year: as great as Agni is, as great as is his measure, by so much he thus kindles him.

Eggeling
  1. He recites both g─Бyatr─л and trishс╣нubh verses; for the g─Бyatr─л metre is the vital air, and the trishс╣нubh is the body (self): by the g─Бyatr─л verses he thus kindles his vital air, and by the trishс╣нubh ones the body. The trishс╣нubh verses are in the middle, and the g─Бyatr─л verses on both sides thereof; for this body is in the middle, and the (organs of) the vital airs are on the sides thereof. He pronounces more g─Бyatr─л verses before, and fewer after (the

trishс╣нubh verses); for there are more (organs of the) vital airs in front, and fewer behind.

рд╕с│Шрдорд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рд╛рдЧреНрди рдЛрддс│Шрд╡реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрдиреНрддреНрд╡рд┐с│Шрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛с│Шрдкрддрд┐рдВ рд╡рд┐с│Шрд╕реНрд░рд╕реНрддрдВ рдпс│ШрддреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГс│Ш рд╕рдос│Шрджрдзрд╛рддреНрддс│ШрдордмреНрд░рд╡реАрджреНрдпрд╛ рдос│ШрддреНрд╕рдВрдорд┐рддрд╛рдГ рд╕рд╛рдорд┐рдзреЗрдиреНрдпс│Шрд╕реНрддрд╛с│Шрднрд┐рд░реНрдорд╛ рд╕с│Шрдорд┐рдиреНрддреНрд╕реНрд╡реЗс│Шрддрд┐рее

рдореВрд▓рдореН - рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдореН

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

рдЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдирд┐рдзреАрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛ рдЛрдЪрд╕реНрддрджрдиреБрд╡рд╛рдЪрдирдВ рд╡рд┐рдзрддреНрддреЗ рд╕реЛ рд╜рдиреНрд╡рд╛рд╣- рд╕рдорд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╜рдЧреНрди рдЛрддрд╡реЛ рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрдпрдВрддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ ред рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдорд░реНрдердВ рд╡рд┐рд╡рдХреНрд╖реБрд╕реНрддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рд╕рдорд┐рдВрдзрдирд╛рд░реНрдерддрд╛рдВ рджрд░реНрд╢рдпрддрд┐- рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ ред рдпрджрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд░рд╕реНрддрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд▓рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдВрдЧрдВ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рдВ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд╕рдорджрдзрд╛рддреН рд╕рдВрдпреЛрдЬрд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рддрдордмреНрд░рд╡реАрддреН рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рд░рд┐рддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рдорддреНрд╕рдВрдорд┐рддрд╛рдГ рдордо рдкрд░реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрд╛рдГ рдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рд╛рдорд┐рдзреЗрдиреНрдпрдГ рддрд╛рднрд┐рдГ ‘рдорд╛’ рдорд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рдВ рд╕рдорд┐рддреНрдиреНрд╕реНрд╡ рд╕рдВрджреАрдкрдпреЗрддрд┐ ред рдЗрдВрдзреЗрд░реНрд▓реЛрдЯрд┐ рдордзреНрдпрдореЗ рд░реВрдкрдореН рее реирел рее

Eggeling
  1. He recites (V─Бj. S. XXVII, 1), ‘May the months 19, O Agni, may the seasons make thee grow!’ When Agni restored the relaxed Praj─Бpati, he (Praj─Бpati) said to him, ‘What kindling-verses there are equal to me (in measure), with them kindle me!’

рдореВрд▓рдореН - рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдореН

рд╕ рдПрддрд╛ рдЕрдкрд╢реНрдпрддреН- “рд╕рдорд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╜рдЧреНрди рдЛрддрд╡реЛ рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрдпрдВрддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐”- рд╕рдорд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╜рдЧреНрди рдЛрддрд╡рд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрдпрдВрддреБ- рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрддрддреН ред “рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рд╛ рдЛрд╖рдпреЛ рдпрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛”- рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рддреНрд╡рд░реНрд╖рдпрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдЪ рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрдпрдВрддреБ- рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрддрддреН ред “рд╕рдВ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпреЗрди рджреАрджрд┐рд╣рд┐ рд░реЛрдЪрдиреЗрди”- рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЕрд╕реМ рд╡рд╛ рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпреЛ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдВ рд░реЛрдЪрдирдВ, рддреЗрди рд╕рдВрджреАрджрд┐рд╣реАрддреНрдпреЗрддрддреН ред “рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдЖрднрд╛рд╣рд┐ рдкреНрд░рджрд┐рд╢рд╢реНрдЪрддрд╕реНрд░рдГ”- (рд╡рд╛реж рд╕рдВреж реирен ред рез) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдЖрднрд╛рд╣рд┐ рдкреНрд░рджрд┐рд╢рд╢реНрдЪрддрд╕реНрд░- рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрддрддреН рее реирем рее

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

рдПрд╡рдореБрдХреНрддреЛ рд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рд╕рдорд┐рдВрдзрдирд╛рд░реНрдердВ рд╕рд╛рдорд┐рдзреЗрдиреАрдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреН рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣- рд╕ рдПрддрд╛ рдЕрдкрд╢реНрдпрддреН- рд╕рдорд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╜рдЧреНрди рдЛрддрд╡реЛ рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрдпрдВрддреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрддрд┐ ред рдЗрддрд┐рд╢рдмреНрджрдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗ ред рдПрд╡рдВрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░рд╛ рдирд╡ рдЛрдЪреЛ рд╜рдкрд╢реНрдпрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ 20 ред рдордВрддреНрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджрдордиреВрджреНрдп рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╖реНрдЯреЗ- рд╕рдорд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╜рдЧреНрди рдЛрддрд╡рд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрдпрдВрддреНрд╡рд┐рддреНрдпреЗрддрджрд┐рддрд┐ рее реирем рее

Eggeling
  1. He (Agni) saw these (verses), ‘May the months, O Agni, may the seasons make thee grow!’ that is, ‘May both the months, O Agni, and the seasons make thee grow!’–‘The years, the R╠еshis, whatsoever truths’ that is, ‘May the years, and the R╠еshis, and the truths make thee grow!’–‘With heavenly brightness do thou shine!’–the heavenly brightness doubtless is yonder sun: thus ’together with that do thou shine!’–’lighten up the whole four regions!’ that is, ’lighten up all the four regions!’

Eggeling
  1. These (verses) have one and the same explanation regarding him (Agni-Praj─Бpati): how one would make him complete, how he would restore and produce him. They relate to Agni and Praj─Бpati: to Agni, inasmuch as Agni saw (them); to Praj─Бpati, inasmuch as he (Agni) kindled Praj─Бpati.

Eggeling
  1. Twelve ─Аpr─л (propitiatory) verses 21 there are,–twelve months are a year, and the year is Agni: as great as Agni is, as great as is his measure, with so much he thus propitiates (or gratifies) him.

Eggeling
  1. And, again, why there are twelve,–of twelve syllables consists the Jagat─л, and the Jagat─л is this earth, for on her there is everything that moves (jag-at) here. Eggeling
  1. And, again, why there are twelve,–of twelve syllables consists the Jagat─л, and the Jagat─л is all the metres, and all the metres are Praj─Бpati (the sacrifice), and Praj─Бpati is Agni: as great as Agni is, as great as is his measure, by so much he thus propitiates him.

Eggeling
  1. He saw these (verses) 22:–‘Upright are his kindling-sticks,’ for upright indeed are the kindling-sticks of him when kindled;–‘upwards tending the bright flashes of Agni,’ for tending upwards are his bright flashes, his flames;–’they, the most brilliant,’ that is ’the most powerful;’–‘of the fair-looking son,’ for fair-looking indeed Agni is on all sides; and inasmuch as he (the Sacrificer) produces him thereby he (Agni) is his son.

Eggeling
  1. These (verses) have one and the same explanation regarding him (Agni-Praj─Бpati): how one would make him complete, how he would restore and produce him. They relate to Agni and Praj─Бpati,–to Agni, inasmuch as Agni saw (them); to Praj─Бpati, inasmuch as he (Agni) propitiated Praj─Бpati.

Eggeling
  1. They are unequal, and consist of unequal feet, and unequal syllables; for the metres are unequal: whatever unequal limbs there are at his (Agni’s) body, those (limbs) of his he propitiates by these (verses).

Eggeling
  1. As to why it belongs to Vai┼Ыv─Бnara;–those layers (of the altar) no doubt are the seasons, for the seasons are the fires; and the seasons are the year, and the year is Vai┼Ыv─Бnara (belonging to all men). Were it (offered) to Agni (Vai┼Ыv─Бnara), he would cause it (the formula) to be redundant. It is one on twelve potsherds: twelve months are a year, and the year is Vai┼Ыv─Бnara. The offering and invitatory formulas relate to Agni, for the obtainment of Agni’s forms. They contain the word ‘k─Бma’ (desire), for the obtainment of his desires.

рдореГрдиреНрдордпрд╛рдиреНрдпреБ рд╣реИрдХреЗ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЙрддреНрд╕рдиреНрдирд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╜рдПрддреЗ рдкрд╢рд╡рдГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡реИ рдХрд┐рдВрдЪреЛрддреНрд╕рдиреНрдирдореН- рдЗрдпрдВ рддрд╕реНрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реНрдард╛ ред рддрджреН рдпрддреНрд░реИрддреЗ рдкрд╢рд╡реЛ рдЧрддрд╛рдГ- рддрдд рдПрдирд╛рдирдзрд┐ рд╕рдореНрднрд░рд╛рдо рдЗрддрд┐ ред рди рддрдерд╛ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдпреЛ рд╡рд╛ рд╜рдПрддреЗрд╖рд╛рдорд╛рд╡реГрддрдВ рдЪ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдВ рдЪ рди рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рддреН- рддрд╕реНрдпреИрдд рд╜рдЙрддреНрд╕рдиреНрдирд╛рдГ рд╕реНрдпреБрдГ ред рд╕ рдПрддрд╛рдиреЗрд╡ рдкрдЮреНрдЪ рдкрд╢реВрдирд╛рд▓рднреЗрдд- рдпрд╛рд╡рджрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╢рдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рддрд╛рдиреНрд╣реИрддрд╛рдиреНрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рдердо рдЖрд▓реЗрднреЗ ред рд╢реНрдпрд╛рдкрд░реНрдгрдГ рд╕рд╛рдпрдХрд╛рдпрдиреЛ рд╜рдиреНрддрдордГ ред рдЕрде рд╣ рд╕реНрдореИрддрд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреНрддрд░реЗрдгрд╛рд▓рднрдиреНрддреЗ ред рдЕрдереИрддрд░реНрд╣реАрдореМ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд╡реЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рднреНрдпреЗрддреЗ- рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдкрддреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ, рд╡рд╛рдпрд╡реНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ ред рддрдпреЛрд░рддреЛ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореБрджреНрдпрддреЗ рее рейрепрее

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

рдореГрдиреНрдордпрд╛рдиреНрдпреБ рд╣реИрдХ рдЗрддрд┐ ред ‘рдПрддреЗ’ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рджрдпрдГ ‘рдкрд╢рд╡рдГ’ ‘рдЙрддреНрд╕рдиреНрдирд╛рдГ’ рдЖрд▓рдмреНрдзрд╡реНрдпрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН, рдЕрддрдГ рдХрд┐рдВ рдореГрдиреНрдордпрдХрд░рдгрдорд┐рддрд┐; рддрддреНрд░рд╛рд╣- рдпрджреНрд╡реИ рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪреЗрддрд┐ ред ‘рдпрддреН рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ рдЙрддреНрд╕рдиреНрдирдВ’ рд╡рд╕реНрддреБ рднрд╡рддрд┐, ‘рддрд╕реНрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп’ ‘рдЗрдпрдВ’ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА- ‘рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реНрдард╛’; рдирд╖реНрдЯрдВ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрдордиреНрд╡реЗрддреАрддрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рддреНрд╡рдореН ред ‘рддрддреН’ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН ‘рдпрддреНрд░’ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдкреНрд░рджреЗрд╢реЗ рдирд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдГ ‘рдкрд╢рд╡рдГ’ ‘рдЧрддрд╛рдГ’, ‘рддрддрдГ’ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рджреЗрд╢рд╛рддреН ‘рдПрдирд╛рдиреН’ рдкрд╢реВрдиреН ‘рд╕рдореНрднрд░рд╛рдордГ’ рдЖрдиреЗрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдордГ ‘рдЗрддрд┐’ рдореГрдиреНрдордпрдХрд░рдгреЗ рдпреБрдХреНрддрд┐рдГ ред рди рддрдерд╛ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рддрд┐ рддрдиреНрдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдГ рее

рдЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдкрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд▓рдореНрднрдкрдХреНрд╖рдВ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдиреНрддрдпрддрд┐- рдпреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдПрддреЗрд╖рд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ ред ‘рдЖрд╡реГрддрдВ’ рдкреНрд░рдпрд╛рдгрдХреНрд░рдордореН, рддрджреНрд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдпрдХрдВ ‘рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН’ ‘рдЪ’ рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖ рдПрд╡ ‘рдПрддреЗ’ рдкрд╢рд╡рдГ ‘рдЙрддреНрд╕рдиреНрдирд╛рдГ’ ред рд╕ рдПрддрд╛рдирд┐рддрд┐ ред ‘рд╕рдГ’ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН ред рдпрд╛рд╡рджрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╢рдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рддрд┐ ред ‘рдЕрд╕реНрдп’ рдЪрд┐рдиреНрд╡рддрдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╕реНрдп ‘рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН’ рдХрд░реНрдордкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧрдГ ‘рд╡рд╢рдГ’ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН ’ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдзреАрдиреЛ рднрд╡реЗрддреН, ‘рд╕ рдкрд╢реВрдирд╛рд▓рднреЗрдд’ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ рее

рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирд░реНрдереЗ рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рддреГрд╕рдореНрдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгрдпрддрд┐- рддрд╛рдиреН рд╣реИрддрд╛рдиреН рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рдердо рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╕рд╛рдпрдХрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрддреНрдпрдВ ‘рд╕рд╛рдпрдХрд╛рдпрдирдГ’ ‘рд╢реНрдпрд╛рдкрд░реНрдгрдГ’ рдирд╛рдо ‘рдЕрдиреНрддрдордГ’ рдЪрд░рдордГ ‘рдЖрд▓реЗрднреЗ’ ред ‘рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реЗрдг’ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рд╢реНрдпрд╛рдкрд░реНрдгрдпреЛрд░рдиреНрддрд░рд╛рд▓рдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рдпреЗ рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рддрд╛рд░рдГ, рддреЗ ‘рдПрддрд╛рдиреЗрд╡’ рдкрдЮреНрдЪ рдкрд╢реВрдиреН ‘рдЖрд▓рднрдиреНрддреЗ’ рдЖрд▓реЗрднрд┐рд░реЗ рее

рдПрддрд╛рд╡рддреНрдкрд░реНрдпрдиреНрддрдВ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдкрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд▓рдореНрднрдкрдХреНрд╖ рдЙрдХреНрддрдГ, рдЗрддрдГ рдкрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдкрддреНрдпрд╡рд╛рдпрд╡реНрдпрдкрдХреНрд╖реМ рд╡рд░реНрдгреНрдпреЗрддреЗ 28 ред рддреНрд░рдпрдГ рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдЕрдкрд┐ рд╕рдорд╡рд┐рдХрд▓реНрдкрд╛рдГ ред рддрддреНрд░реЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдордкрд┐ рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рддреГрднрд┐рдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдкрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд▓рдореНрднрдГ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдп рдЗрддрд┐ рдордиреНрдпрддреЗ, рддрд╛рдиреН рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣- рдЕрдереИрддрд░реНрд╣реАрдореМ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд╡реЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рднреНрдпреЗрддреЗ рдЗрддрд┐ ред ‘рдЕрде’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдиреНрддрд░рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░рдореНрднреЗ ред ‘рдПрддрд░реНрд╣рд┐’ рдЕрдзреБрдирд╛ ред рдПрддрдЪреНрдЫрдмреНрджрд╛рддреН рдХрд╛рд▓рд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рд░реНрд╣рд┐рд▓реН рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ ред (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рел ред рей ред резрем) ‘рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдкрддреНрдпрдГ рд╡рд╛рдпрд╡реНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡реМ рдкрд╢реВ ‘рдЖрд▓рднреНрдпреЗрддреЗ’ ред рддрд╛рд╡рдкрд┐ рд╕рдорд╡рд┐рдХрд▓реНрдкрд╛рд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЧреБрдХреНрддрдореН ред ‘рдЕрддрдГ’ ‘рддрдпреЛрдГ’ рдПрддрдпреЛрдГ рдкрд╢реНрд╡реЛрдГ рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдпрдХрдВ ‘рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН’ ‘рдЙрджреНрдпрддреЗ’ рднрдгреНрдпрддреЗ ред “рд╡рдж рд╡реНрдпрдХреНрддрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрд┐” (рдзрд╛. рдкрд╛. рднреНрд╡рд╛. рдк. резрежрейрек) рд▓рд┐рдЯрд┐ “рд╡рдЪрд┐рд╕реНрд╡рдкрд┐рдпрдЬрд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рдХрд┐рддрд┐”- (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рем ред рез ред резрел) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдореНрдкреНрд░рд╕рд╛рд░рдгрдореН рее рейреп рее

рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрд╕рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рдорд╛рдзрд╡реАрдпреЗ рд╡реЗрджрд╛рд░реНрдердкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдиреНрджрд┐рдиреАрдпрд╢рддрдкрдердмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рд╖рд╖реНрдардХрд╛рдгреНрдбреЗ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпреЗ рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН рее (рем-реи-рез) рее

Eggeling
  1. Some, again, make earthen ones, thinking, ‘Passed away, forsooth, are these animals, and this earth is the shelter of all that has passed away: thus whither those animals have gone, from thence we collect them.’ Let him not do so, for whoso knows not both the practice and theory of these (victims), for him let them be passed away. Let him slaughter those very five victims, as far as he may be able to do so; for it was these Praj─Бpati was the first to slaughter, and ┼Ъy─Бparс╣Зa S─Бyak─Бyana the last; and in the interval also people used to slaughter them. But nowadays only these two are slaughtered, the one for Praj─Бpati, and the one for V─Бyu. The theory of these two is now (to be) told.

  1. 162:1 Or, I will make them part of mine own self.–Similarly St. Petersburg dictionary, ‘I will change them into myself.’ But differently Professor Delbr├╝ck, Altind. Synt., p. 239, ‘I will make myself to be these, change myself into these.’ This is on account of the middle form of the verb, which, however, is quite justified also in the former interpretation. Cf. VI, 8, 2, 1, where there is no question of changing the whole sacrifice into a heap of ashes, but of taking over the ashes, or some of it, to form part of the sacrifice. ↩︎

  2. рдкрд░рд┐рд╡реГрддреЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрдкрдирдВ ред рдЕрдЬрд╕реНрдп рд╢реБрдВрдзрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдЪрд░рдгрдпреЛрдЧрд╛рддреН ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛ рд╜рд╡реНрд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╛рддреН ред рд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреНрдпреЛ рд╡рд╛ ред рдХрд╛. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рд╕реВ. резрем ред резрек-резрен ред ↩︎

  3. рдХрдВрдареЗрд╖реБ рддреГрдгрдордВрддрд░реНрджреНрдзрд╛рдп рд╢рд┐рд░рд╛рдБрд╕реНрдпрд╛рджрддреНрддреЗ ред рдХрд╛реж рд╢реНрд░реМреж рд╕реВреж ред резрем ред резрео ↩︎ ↩︎

  4. “рд╢реНрд░реЛрдгреА рдпрджреВрд░реВ рдХ рдЙ рддрдЬреНрдЬрдЬрд╛рди рддрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдХреБрд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзрдВ рд╕реБрджреГрдврдВ рдмрднреВрд╡” рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдереж рд╕рдВреж резреж-реи-рей ред ↩︎

  5. 163:1 See VI, 1, 1, 4. ↩︎

  6. 163:2 That is, on the fire-altar, or (which is the same thing) on himself, Praj─Бpati, the sacrifice. The heads of the five victims are placed in (a dish introduced into) the bottom layer of the altar so as to impart stability to it. See VII, 5, 2, 1 seq. ↩︎

  10. 164:1 S─Бyaс╣Зa explains ‘abhisaс╣Бskarishye’ by ‘─Бdhiyaj├▒ike ┼Ыar─лra upadh─Бsy─Бmi,’ ‘if I were to put this (clay and water) on the sacrificial body.’ ↩︎

  11. 164:2 A play on the word which may mean either ’non-bricks,’ or ‘being without oblation (ishс╣нa).’ ↩︎

  12. 164:3 S─Бyaс╣Зa seems to take this to mean, that animals (cattle) delight, or sport, when the sacrificial fire is established; that is to say, they feel at home and increase wherever a new household is established (?);–tasm─Бd agn─Бv ─Бhite pa┼Ыavo ramante, ─Бtmany eva s─Б pr─лtir ity abhipr─Бyaс╕е. Adhun─Бgneс╕е pa┼Ыushv ─Бtmabh┼лteshu pr─лtiс╣Б dar┼Ыayann ─Бha, yasm─Бd agnir esha yat pa┼Ыavas tasm─Бd yasya manushyasya pa┼Ыavo bhavanti tasminn etad agnir ─Бdh─лyate, tatra hi sa ─Бtmabh┼лtaiс╕е pa┼Ыubh─л ramate n─Бnyatra; evam yad agny─Бtmik─Бс╕е pa┼Ыavas tatas tam agnim ─Бtm─Бbhisaс╣Бskr╠еtya praj─Бpatir agnir abhavat. ↩︎

  17. 167:1 For the eleven g─Бyatr─л verses, used as s─Бmidhen─лs at an ordinary ishс╣нi–and raised to the number of fifteen by repetitions of the first and last verses–see part i, p. 102. The present animal sacrifice (ishс╣нak─Б-pa┼Ыu) adds to these verses nine trishс╣нubh verses (V─Бj. S. XXVII, 1-9), which (according to K─Бty. XVI, 1, 11) are to be inserted between the two verses containing the words ‘samidhyam─Бna’ (being kindled) and ‘samiddha’ (kindled) respectively,–that is, between the ninth and tenth of the normal or g─Бyatr─л kindling-verses (cf. I, 4, 1, 38). ↩︎

  18. 167:2 See VI, 1, 1, 15; 3, 19. ↩︎

  19. 168:1 This is the meaning assigned here to ‘sam─Бс╕е’ by Mah─лdhara, a doubtful meaning indeed. Besides the ordinary meaning year,’ the St. Petersburg dictionary also allows to ‘sam─Б’ that of ‘half-year’ in some passages of the Atharva-veda. In the present passage, the dictionary refers ‘sam─Бс╕е’ to the adjective ‘sama,’ hence ’the equal seasons.’ This cannot, however, have been the meaning assigned to the word by the author of this part of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, whatever it may originally have been in this verse of the Saс╣Бhit─Бs. S─Бyaс╣Зa, Taitt. S. IV, 1, 7, takes ‘sam─Бс╕е’ in the sense of ’the years,’ but remarks that ’the months and half-months’ have to be understood by it in this verse. ↩︎
